        This test file demonstrates the evolution from mocked dialog tests to real

        initialization bugs, UI state bugs, and cross-dialog communication issues.
        
        CRITICAL DIFFERENCES FROM MOCKED VERSION:

        2. REAL manager integration with dialog workflows
        3. REAL UI component validation and interaction testing
        4. REAL dialog-controller-manager integration chains
        5. REAL error propagation through dialog boundaries
        
        This replaces mock usage in dialog tests:
        - Mock file dialogs and UI components (hides real initialization bugs)
        - Mock manager integration (can't test real dialog-manager coordination)
        - Mock Qt parent/child relationships (misses real Qt lifecycle issues)
        - Mock signal connections (can't test real cross-dialog communication)
        
        NOTE: Uses REAL dialog instantiation which can be sensitive in Qt offscreen mode.
        If these tests fail in offscreen, use @pytest.mark.requires_display or adjust
        the dialog expectations to match headless behavior.

        <Class TestRoundTripModification>
          Tests for sprite modification and reinjection.
          <Function test_modify_tile_and_reinject>
            Full round-trip: extract, modify a tile, reinject, verify.
            
            This test:
            1. Extracts a sprite from ROM
            2. Modifies an entire 8x8 tile (32 bytes) with a checkerboard pattern
            3. Creates a PNG with the modified data
            4. Reinjects the modified sprite (with force=True since compression may vary)
            5. Re-extracts and verifies the modification persisted
            
            Note: force=True is used because HAL compression is not deterministic -
            the same data may compress to slightly different sizes. The test ROM copy
            is isolated in tmp_path, so force injection is safe here.
          <Function test_rom_checksum_updated_after_injection>
            Verify ROM checksum is recalculated after injection.

          <Function test_extraction_at_various_offsets_deterministic>
            Verify extraction behavior is consistent at different offsets.
            
            Some offsets may have valid HAL-compressed data (the ROM format reuses
            HAL compression for various data types), so this test verifies that
            extraction is deterministic rather than testing for failure.

      <Module test_smart_preview.py>
        <Function test_smart_preview_initialization>
          Verify PreviewGenerator can be initialized.
        <Class TestBackgroundPreloadStalenessCheck>
          Tests for background preload handling in SmartPreviewCoordinator.
          
          Bug: Background preloads use negative request_ids to differentiate them
          from user-triggered requests. However, the staleness check
          `if request_id < self._request_counter` always rejects negative IDs
          since _request_counter is always non-negative.
          
          This defeats the background preloading optimization entirely.
          <Function test_negative_request_id_not_treated_as_stale>
            BUG REPRODUCTION: Negative request IDs should NOT be rejected as stale.
            
            Background preloads use negative request_ids (-1001, -1002, etc.) to
            differentiate them from user-triggered requests. The staleness check
            should only apply to positive IDs.
            
            This test will FAIL before the fix is applied.
          <Function test_positive_request_id_staleness_check_still_works>
            Positive request IDs should still be checked for staleness normally.
            
            This ensures the fix doesn't break the normal staleness detection.
        <Class TestCachePoisoningPrevention>
          Tests for cache key correctness in background preload handling.
          
          Bug (Issue 1 from desync report): Background preloads used self._current_offset
          for the cache key instead of actual_offset, causing cache poisoning when
          the user changed offsets before a background preload completed.
          
          Scenario:
          1. User viewing offset 0x010000 (_current_offset = 0x010000)
          2. Background preload requests offset 0x020000 (does NOT update _current_offset)
          3. Worker completes with data for 0x020000
          4. BUG: Cache stores under key 0x010000 instead of 0x020000
          5. Cache is now corrupted - offset 0x010000 has wrong data
          <Function test_background_preload_uses_actual_offset_for_cache_key>
            BUG REPRODUCTION: Background preload should cache under actual_offset, not _current_offset.
            
            This test will FAIL before the fix is applied.
          <Function test_user_request_still_caches_correctly>
            User-triggered requests (positive IDs) should still cache correctly.
            
            Ensures the fix doesn't break normal user-triggered caching.

    <Module test_slack_detection.py>
      Tests for ROM injector slack detection functionality.
      
      Slack detection identifies padding bytes (0xFF or 0x00) between compressed
      sprites in ROM data. This is important for injection to know how much
      space is available without relocating data.
      
      Refactored from unittest.TestCase to pytest for consistency with the rest
      of the test suite.
      <Function test_slack_detection[ff_padding]>
        Verify slack detection correctly identifies padding bytes.
        
        Slack bytes are 0xFF or 0x00 padding between compressed sprites.
        Detection is capped at MAX_SLACK_SIZE to avoid false positives.
        
        Args:
            rom_injector: Fixture providing mocked ROMInjector
            slack_bytes: Padding bytes to insert after compressed data
            expected_slack_size: Expected detected slack size
            description: Test case description for debugging
      <Function test_slack_detection[zero_padding]>
        Verify slack detection correctly identifies padding bytes.
        
        Slack bytes are 0xFF or 0x00 padding between compressed sprites.
        Detection is capped at MAX_SLACK_SIZE to avoid false positives.
        
        Args:
            rom_injector: Fixture providing mocked ROMInjector
            slack_bytes: Padding bytes to insert after compressed data
            expected_slack_size: Expected detected slack size
            description: Test case description for debugging
      <Function test_slack_detection[no_slack]>
        Verify slack detection correctly identifies padding bytes.
        
        Slack bytes are 0xFF or 0x00 padding between compressed sprites.
        Detection is capped at MAX_SLACK_SIZE to avoid false positives.
        
        Args:
            rom_injector: Fixture providing mocked ROMInjector
            slack_bytes: Padding bytes to insert after compressed data

        <Module test_delete_later_cleanup.py>
          Regression test for processEvents() availability in offscreen mode.
          
          This test verifies that processEvents() is called in offscreen mode.
          Previously, IS_HEADLESS incorrectly treated offscreen as "no Qt",
          causing processEvents() to be skipped in fixture cleanup.
          
          The fix ensures that event processing runs whenever a QApplication exists,
          which is required for Qt cleanup mechanisms (deleteLater, signal queuing, etc).
          <Class TestProcessEventsInOffscreen>
            Verify processEvents() works in offscreen mode.
            
            Regression: IS_HEADLESS was True for offscreen mode, causing fixture
            cleanup to skip processEvents(). This prevented Qt cleanup mechanisms
            from running at all in CI environments.
            <Function test_qapplication_exists_in_offscreen>
              QApplication should exist and be usable in offscreen mode.
            <Function test_process_events_is_callable>
              processEvents() should be callable without error in offscreen mode.
            <Function test_can_create_and_schedule_deletion>
              Can create Qt objects and schedule them for deletion.
            <Function test_signals_can_be_queued_and_processed>
              Queued signal connections should work in offscreen mode.
          <Class TestEnvironmentDetection>
            Verify environment detection distinguishes offscreen from headless.
            <Function test_offscreen_is_not_headless>
              Offscreen mode should NOT be considered headless.
              
              Headless = no Qt at all
              Offscreen = Qt works, just no physical display
            <Function test_qt_is_available_in_offscreen>

        <Module test_auto_align_zoom.py>
          Tests for WorkbenchCanvas auto-align zoom behavior.
          
          Bug: When auto-alignment produces a large offset, fitInView zooms out too much
          and frames become effectively invisible (appear as tiny dots).
          
          This test specifically reproduces the "frames disappear" scenario where the AI
          frame has content far from its origin, causing auto-align to produce a large
          negative offset. The union of the game and AI frame rects becomes very large,
          and fitInView zooms out excessively.
          <Class TestAutoAlignZoomBehavior>
            Tests for excessive zoom-out bug during auto-alignment.
            <Function test_auto_align_keeps_frames_visible_with_large_offset>
              Auto-align should not zoom out excessively when offset is large.
              
              Scenario:
              - Game frame: 64x64 at canvas origin (0, 0)
              - AI frame: 1024x1024 with VERY SMALL content far from origin
              - Content at (900, 900) to (950, 950) - 50x50 pixels
              - Auto-align will center this tiny content over game frame
              - Expected offset: extremely large and negative (~-900, -900)
              - BUG: fitInView on united rect zooms way out, frames become dots
            <Function test_auto_align_normal_offset_shows_both_frames>
              Auto-align with reasonable offset should show both frames (baseline test).
              
              This test ensures the fix doesn't break normal cases where offset is small.
        <Module test_canvas_alignment_sync.py>

          _on_alignment_updated only updates the mapping panel drawer. The canvas
          still shows the old position.

        <Module test_transform_persistence.py>
          Tests for transform persistence when switching between AI frames.
          
          Bug: Scale changes are lost when moving to a different AI frame and back.
          Offset and flip changes persist correctly because their handlers call
          _emit_alignment_changed(), but _on_scale_slider_changed did not.
          <Class TestScalePersistence>
            Tests for scale transform persistence via alignment_changed signal.
            <Function test_scale_slider_emits_alignment_changed>
              Scale slider change should emit alignment_changed signal.
              
              Bug: _on_scale_slider_changed() did not call _emit_alignment_changed(),
              so scale changes were never persisted to the mapping.
              
              This test verifies that changing the scale slider emits the signal
              that triggers persistence to the project mapping.
            <Function test_scale_persistence_matches_flip_pattern>
              Scale handler should follow the same emit pattern as flip handler.
              
              Both _on_flip_changed and _on_scale_slider_changed should emit
              alignment_changed signal to persist transforms.
              
              Note: Slider range is 10-100 (0.1x to 1.0x), so we use 50 (0.5x).
            <Function test_scale_changes_trigger_preview_update>
              Scale changes should schedule preview update like flip changes.
              
              _on_flip_changed calls _schedule_preview_update() to update the
              in-game preview. _on_scale_slider_changed should do the same.
        <Module test_workflow_fixes.py>
          Tests for frame mapping workflow fixes.
          
          Covers:

          - Step 3: Auto-save after structural changes
          - Step 4: Controller-routed compression updates

            Step 5: Verify canvas state is preserved during content updates.
            <Function test_project_changed_preserves_canvas_on_content_update>
              Canvas should not clear when project content changes (same project).
              
              Only clear on new/load project (identity change).
          <Class TestSplitBrainFixes>
            Step 6: Verify canvas/selection split brain fixes.
            
            The workspace tracks two distinct IDs:
            - _selected_game_id: What user last clicked in the captures library
            - _current_canvas_game_id: What the canvas is actually displaying
            
            These can differ when previewing captures. The fixes ensure:
            1. Compression changes apply to the displayed frame (canvas), not selected
            2. Blocked alignment edits show user feedback
            <Function test_compression_type_applied_to_canvas_frame_not_selected>
              Compression changes should apply to canvas frame, not selected frame.
              
              Scenario:
              1. AI frame mapped to capture_a (selected_game_id = capture_a)
              2. User clicks capture_b to preview (canvas shows capture_b)
              3. User changes compression type
              4. Compression should apply to capture_b (what canvas shows), not capture_a
              
              Bug: _on_compression_type_changed used _selected_game_id instead of
              _current_canvas_game_id, causing compression to apply to the wrong frame.
            <Function test_alignment_blocked_shows_user_feedback>
              When alignment edit is blocked, user should get status bar feedback.
              
              Scenario:
              1. AI frame mapped to capture_a
              2. User clicks capture_b to preview (canvas shows capture_b)
              3. User drags AI frame to adjust alignment
              4. Alignment edit should be blocked AND user should see a message
              
              Bug: Alignment was silently blocked with no user feedback, causing
              confusion when users tried to adjust alignment.

            <Class TestFilterClearsSelectionSignal>
              Tests for filter behavior when hiding selected items.
              
              Design: Pane does NOT emit empty string when filter hides selection.
              The workspace state manager is the source of truth for selection,
              and panes should not clear external state when filters hide items.

            <Class TestProjectReloadSignaling>
              Tests for Phase 2 bug: silent selection restoration after project reload.
              
              Bug: When project is reloaded (set_ai_frames called with new frame list),
              selection that was preserved should emit signal to notify listeners (like canvas).
              Currently blocks signals, restores silently, then unblocks - workspace never knows
              selection was restored, leaving canvas showing stale data.
              
              Signal migration: Now emits frame ID (filename) instead of index.

                Auto-align should show both frames in the actual viewport (not just scene rect).

                and the viewport is smaller than the scene. fitInView() is needed instead.
            <Class TestAutoAlignCoordinates>
              Tests for Bug #4: Initial auto-align uses wrong bounding box coordinates.
              
              Bug: _attempt_link() passes capture bounding box x,y (screen coordinates)
              to calculate_auto_alignment(), but the canvas displays the game frame at (0,0).
              This causes large incorrect offsets when the capture position != (0,0).
              
              The fix: Always use (0, 0) for game_bbox_x/y since that's where the game frame
              is displayed on the canvas.
              <Function test_auto_alignment_uses_canvas_origin_not_capture_position>
                Auto-alignment should calculate offset relative to canvas origin (0,0).
                
                When a sprite is captured at screen position (120, 80), the bounding box
                will have x=120, y=80. But on the canvas, the game frame is always displayed
                at (0, 0). The alignment offset must be calculated relative to (0, 0).
                
                This test FAILS until _attempt_link is fixed to use (0, 0) instead of bbox.x/y.

        <Module test_arrangement_workflow.py>
          Consolidated Arrangement Workflow Tests.
          
          This file consolidates all arrangement-related regression tests from:
          - test_arrangement_canvas_preservation.py (4 tests)
          - test_arrangement_defaults.py (2 tests)
          - test_arrangement_overlay_fixes.py (10 tests)
          - test_arrangement_persistence_integration.py (2 tests)

            <Function test_arrangement_config_persists_overlay_scale>

          <Class TestApplyOperation>
            Tests for overlay apply operation behavior.
            
            Source: test_arrangement_overlay_fixes.py
            <Function test_apply_operation_replaces_partially_covered_tiles>
              Regression test: ApplyOperation must completely REPLACE partially covered tiles (no composition).
            <Function test_opaque_black_not_quantized_to_transparent_index>
              Regression test: Opaque black pixels should NOT become transparent.
              
              BUG: When an overlay has opaque black pixels (0,0,0,255), they get quantized
              to palette index 0 (which is typically black in SNES palettes). But index 0
              is reserved for transparency in SNES sprites, so these pixels appear transparent.
              
              FIX: When quantizing opaque pixels, skip index 0 entirely.
            <Function test_transparent_pixels_remain_transparent>
              Regression test: Transparent pixels in overlay should become transparent in output.
          <Class TestDuplicateTilePrevention>
            Tests for duplicate tile placement prevention.
            
            Source: test_arrangement_overlay_fixes.py - Risk 1 tests
            
            When the same tile key is already placed on the canvas,
            attempting to place it at a different position should fail.
            <Function test_duplicate_tile_placement_rejected>
              Risk 1: Same physical tile placed at multiple canvas positions should be rejected.
            <Function test_move_tile_allows_same_key>
              Moving a tile (remove + place) should work even though key is 'duplicate'.

        <Module test_mesen_capture_offset_handling.py>
          Consolidated tests for Mesen capture offset handling.
          
          This module combines tests previously spread across multiple files:
          - Offset hunting algorithm (DMA jitter correction)
          - FILE ↔ ROM offset normalization (SMC header handling)
          - Capture list widget updates
          - Cross-component coordination
          
          Related:
          - ui/components/panels/recent_captures_widget.py - Widget being tested
          - ui/rom_extraction/widgets/mesen_captures_section.py - Section wrapper
          - core/offset_hunting.py - Offset candidate generation
          <Class TestOriginalOffsetPreferred>
            Test that original offset is used when decompression succeeds.
            
            Bug: clicking 0x293AEB opens 0x293AED - original offset should be trusted
            when HAL decompression succeeds, regardless of has_nonzero_content() result.
            <Function test_original_offset_used_despite_low_nonzero_content>
              Bug: clicking 0x293AEB opens 0x293AED - original should be used.
              
              Scenario:
              1. User clicks Mesen capture at offset 0x293AEB
              2. HAL decompression succeeds at 0x293AEB (valid sprite data)
              3. But has_nonzero_content() returns False (sprite is mostly black)
              4. Bug: Loop continues to 0x293AED which also succeeds and passes check
              5. Result: Editor opens at wrong offset
              
              Expected behavior:
              - If original offset decompresses successfully, use it immediately
              - Don't apply has_nonzero_content() to the PRIMARY offset
            <Function test_has_nonzero_content_threshold_behavior>
              Document has_nonzero_content behavior for edge cases.
            <Function test_mostly_black_sprite_is_valid>
              Verify that a mostly-black sprite should still be extracted.
              
              A sprite with mostly black pixels (transparent in many SNES games)
              is still a valid sprite. has_nonzero_content was designed to filter
              GARBAGE data, not valid mostly-transparent sprites.
          <Class TestPreviewWorkerOffsetSelection>
            Test that PreviewWorkerPool uses original offset when valid.
            <Function test_original_offset_preferred_when_decompression_succeeds>
              Verify original offset is used even if has_nonzero_content would fail.
            <Function test_offset_hunting_flow_integration>
              Integration test for offset hunting with the fix applied.
            <Function test_preview_worker_prefers_primary_offset_when_ratio_check_rejects>
              Bug repro: preview worker should not skip primary offset due to ratio validation.
          <Class TestOffsetHuntingPurpose>
            Document the intended purpose of offset hunting.
            <Function test_offset_hunting_is_for_dma_jitter_not_validation>
              Offset hunting exists to correct DMA timing jitter, not to improve quality.
              
              When Mesen Lua captures a sprite's DMA address, slight timing variations
              can cause the captured offset to be off by a few bytes. The offset hunting
              mechanism tries nearby offsets to find the correct HAL compression header.
              
              IMPORTANT: The original offset from Lua should be trusted if decompression
              succeeds. We should NOT skip it just because the decompressed data has low
              entropy or is mostly black.
            <Function test_has_nonzero_content_purpose>
              has_nonzero_content is meant to detect GARBAGE, not filter valid sprites.
              
              The check was added to avoid accepting data that:
              1. Decompresses to all zeros (corrupt or wrong offset)
              2. Is random noise that happens to decompress
              
              It should NOT reject valid sprites that happen to be mostly black/transparent.
              The fix: Only apply has_nonzero_content to ALTERNATE offsets, not the original.
          <Class TestCaptureOffsetAdjustment>
            Test alignment adjustment signal flow when HAL alignment corrects offset.
            <Function test_alignment_adjustment_updates_capture_list>
              Verify that alignment adjustments update the capture list display.
              
              Scenario:
              1. User clicks on Mesen capture at ROM offset 0x3C7071
              2. Preview worker compresses with HAL, discovers sprite at offset 0x3C7075
              3. ROMWorkflowController emits capture_offset_adjusted(0x3C7071, 0x3C7075)
              4. RecentCapturesWidget.update_capture_offset receives adjustment
          <Class TestSMCOffsetNormalization>
            Test SMC header offset handling for captures.
            <Function test_captures_added_before_rom_load_get_renormalized>
              Verify that captures added before ROM load are re-normalized correctly.
              
              Scenario:
              1. Mesen discovers sprite at FILE offset 0x3C7271 (before ROM loads)
              2. RecentCapturesWidget adds capture with SMC offset 0
              3. Capture stores ROM offset as 0x3C7271 (FILE - 0 = FILE)
              4. User loads KSSU ROM, set_smc_offset(512) called
              5. Existing captures should be re-normalized
            <Function test_multiple_captures_added_before_rom_load>
              Verify that multiple captures are all re-normalized when SMC offset changes.
          <Class TestOffsetNormalizationEdgeCases>
            Edge cases for offset normalization.
            <Function test_non_smc_rom_no_normalization>
              Verify that non-SMC ROMs don't normalize offsets.
            <Function test_offset_below_smc_header_not_adjusted>
              Verify that offsets below SMC header size are not adjusted.
            <Function test_update_capture_offset_returns_false_for_missing_offset>
              Verify that update_capture_offset returns False when offset not found.

        <Module test_signal_connection_patterns.py>
          Qt Signal Connection Pattern Tests.
          
          Tests for Qt signal connection patterns and best practices used throughout the codebase.
          These tests use mock workers to verify PATTERNS (not production classes) including:
          - _signals_connected flag synchronization (prevents duplicate connections)
          - blockSignals() usage during cleanup
          - QueuedConnection for cross-thread signals
          - disconnect-before-reconnect patterns
          
          NOTE: This file tests signal connection PATTERNS, not production BatchThumbnailWorker
          or PreviewWorkerPool classes directly. For production class testing, see:
          - tests/integration/test_batch_thumbnail_worker_integration.py
          - tests/ui/integration/test_preview_worker_pool.py (if it exists)
          
          The patterns tested here mirror those in:
          - preview_worker_pool.py:447-450, 532-535 - _signals_connected flag management
          - batch_thumbnail_worker.py:817-819 - signal connection lifecycle
          
          Async Safety Notes
          ------------------
          These tests involve real threaded workers and MUST use qtbot.waitSignal():
          
              with qtbot.waitSignal(worker.preview_ready, timeout=worker_timeout()):
                  pool.submit_request(...)
          
          Without the context manager, signals may emit before the wait starts (race condition).
          
          Key Patterns:
          1. Connect spies BEFORE starting async operations
          2. Use MultiSignalRecorder for multi-signal tracking
          3. Use timeouts from tests/fixtures/timeouts.py
          4. Clean up workers in fixture teardown to prevent thread leaks
          <Class TestPreviewWorkerPoolSignalFlags>
            Test _signals_connected flag behavior in PreviewWorkerPool-like scenarios.
            
            These tests verify the pattern used in preview_worker_pool.py:447-450 and 532-535.
            <Function test_signals_connected_flag_set_on_first_connection>
              _signals_connected flag must be True after first connection.
            <Function test_duplicate_connection_prevented_by_flag>
              Flag should prevent duplicate signal connections on worker reuse.
            <Function test_flag_desync_causes_missed_signals>
              Demonstrate bug: if flag is True but no connection, signals are missed.
            <Function test_flag_must_be_reset_on_cleanup>
              _signals_connected flag must be reset when worker is cleaned up.
          <Class TestPreviewWorkerPoolReuse>
            Test worker reuse patterns from preview_worker_pool.py.
            <Function test_worker_return_to_pool_signals_remain_connected>
              Workers returned to pool should keep signals connected (critical fix).
            <Function test_pool_connection_idempotent_across_requests>
              Multiple submit_request calls should not create duplicate connections.
          <Class TestBatchThumbnailWorkerSignals>
            Test signal connection patterns in batch_thumbnail_worker.py.
            
            Tests the pattern at batch_thumbnail_worker.py:817-819.
            <Function test_start_worker_connects_signals>
              start_worker must connect all required signals.
            <Function test_restart_worker_creates_fresh_connections>
              Restarting worker should create new worker with new connections.
            <Function test_worker_controller_lifecycle_signals>
              Test proper signal lifecycle: started -> progress -> finished.
          <Class TestSignalConnectionPatterns>
            Test and document correct signal connection patterns.
            <Function test_connection_with_type_prevents_race>
              Using QueuedConnection type is safer for cross-thread signals.
            <Function test_disconnect_before_reconnect_pattern>
              Proper pattern: always disconnect before reconnecting.
            <Function test_blockSignals_during_cleanup>
              blockSignals(True) during cleanup prevents unexpected emissions.

        <Module test_widget_contracts.py>
          Widget Signal Contract Tests
          
          This module consolidates all UI widget signal contract tests. These tests verify
          ONLY observable signal behavior:
          - Signal emission count
          - Signal argument values
          - Signal emission order
          - Signal forwarding from child widgets
          
          They do NOT inspect internal state or private attributes.
          The tests should FAIL if the UI stops emitting expected public signals,
          even if internal state changes still occur.
          
          Widgets covered:
          - IconToolbar: Tool selection, zoom, grid toggles, background selection
          - InjectTab: Inject/Save buttons, browse actions
          - PalettePanel: Color selection, source changes, button forwarding
          - PixelCanvas: Mouse interactions, hover, zoom
          - SpriteAssetBrowser: Selection, activation, context menu actions

        <Module test_worker_signal_lifecycle.py>
          Worker signal lifecycle tests.
          
          Tests verifying that worker signals emit in the correct order:
          - started -> progress -> finished
          - Error paths: started -> error -> finished
          
          Also tests known issues from Tier 2:
          - _signals_connected flag desync (preview_worker_pool.py:447-450, 532-535)
          - Signals not disconnected before reconnect (batch_thumbnail_worker.py:817-819)
          
          These tests focus on signal ordering and lifecycle, not full worker functionality.
          
          Async Safety Notes
          ------------------
          These tests use mock workers with synchronous `run_sync()` methods to test signal
          ordering without threading complexity. This is safe because:
          1. MockWorkerWithLifecycle emits signals synchronously in the test thread
          2. processEvents() ensures any queued side-effects complete
          
          For testing REAL threaded workers, use `qtbot.waitSignal()` with context manager:
          
              # REAL ASYNC WORKER PATTERN:
              with qtbot.waitSignal(worker.finished, timeout=worker_timeout()):
                  worker.start()  # Runs in separate thread
          
              # Verify order using MultiSignalRecorder connected BEFORE starting
              recorder = MultiSignalRecorder()
              recorder.connect_signal(worker.started, "started")
              recorder.connect_signal(worker.finished, "finished")
          
              with qtbot.waitSignal(worker.finished, timeout=worker_timeout()):
                  worker.start()
          
              recorder.assert_contains_sequence(["started", "finished"])
          
          IMPORTANT: When testing real threaded workers, connect spies BEFORE starting
          the worker, otherwise signals may be missed.
          <Class TestWorkerLifecycleOrder>
            Test that worker signals emit in correct order.
            <Function test_successful_worker_emits_started_progress_finished>
              Worker must emit started -> progress -> finished in order.
            <Function test_error_worker_emits_started_error_finished>
              Worker with error must emit started -> error -> finished.
            <Function test_finished_always_emitted_last>
              finished signal must always be the last signal emitted.
          <Class TestWorkerProgressTracking>
            Test progress signal emissions.
            <Function test_progress_emits_correct_values>
              Progress signal must emit with correct (current, total) values.
            <Function test_zero_progress_steps_still_emits_lifecycle>
              Worker with no work should still emit started -> finished.
          <Class TestSignalConnectionFlagConsistency>

            - preview_worker_pool.py:447-450, 532-535

            test behavior (signal emission -> slot called) instead of connection counts.

            - batch_thumbnail_worker.py:817-819 (signals not disconnected before reconnect)

            Test signal isolation between multiple worker instances.

              Signals from one worker must not affect another worker's receivers.
            <Function test_no_cross_talk_on_same_signal_name>
              Workers with same signal names must not cross-talk.
          <Class TestAsyncWaitingPatterns>
            Examples demonstrating proper qtbot.waitSignal() usage for async workers.
            
            These tests demonstrate the CORRECT patterns for testing real threaded workers.
            The key principles are:
            1. Always use context manager: `with qtbot.waitSignal(...)`
            2. Connect spies BEFORE starting async operation
            3. Use timeouts from tests/fixtures/timeouts.py
            4. Use `raising=True` to fail fast on timeout (default in pytest-qt)
            <Function test_wait_signal_context_manager_pattern>
              Demonstrate correct context manager pattern for async signals.
              
              CORRECT PATTERN:
                  with qtbot.waitSignal(signal, timeout=timeout):
                      start_async_operation()
              
              WRONG PATTERN (race condition):
                  spy = QSignalSpy(signal)
                  start_async_operation()
                  # Signal may have already emitted before spy was ready!
            <Function test_multiple_signals_with_recorder_and_wait>
              Demonstrate recording multiple signals from async worker.
              
              Pattern: Connect MultiSignalRecorder BEFORE starting, then wait
              for the terminal signal (usually `finished`).
            <Function test_timeout_handling_with_raising>
              Demonstrate timeout handling - test should fail fast on timeout.
              
              By default pytest-qt uses raising=True, meaning TimeoutError is raised
              if the signal isn't emitted within the timeout. This is the correct
              behavior for detecting "signal never emitted" bugs.

          <Class TestPalettePreservationOnPartialOverlay>
            Tests for palette preservation when overlay modifies only some tiles.
            <Function test_get_arrangement_result_only_returns_actually_modified_tiles>
              REGRESSION TEST: get_arrangement_result() must only return tiles that were
              actually modified by the overlay, not ALL tiles.
              
              Bug: After applying overlay to tile (0,0), get_arrangement_result() returns
              all 4 tiles. When _update_tile_data_from_modified_tiles() processes them,
              it assumes all are L-mode (index * 16), but unmodified tiles are P-mode,
              causing palette corruption.
              
              Fix: Track which positions were actually modified and only return those.
            <Function test_multiple_apply_operations_accumulate_modified_positions>
              When overlay is applied multiple times, modified positions should accumulate.
              
              This tests the tracking mechanism: if user applies overlay at (0,0), then
              moves overlay and applies at (0,1), both positions should be tracked.
            <Function test_unmodified_tiles_preserve_original_format>
              Tiles not modified by overlay should preserve their original format.
              
              This is a behavioral test: we verify that tiles not in modified_tiles
              still have their original pixel values.

          Tests for asset browser offset display synchronization.
          <Class TestAssetBrowserOffsetUpdate>
            Tests for asset browser offset display updates.
            <Function test_update_sprite_offset_updates_display_text_with_frame>
              Bug: Asset browser display text doesn't update when offset is adjusted.
              
              Scenario: A Mesen capture with offset 0x293AEB and frame F1938 is added.
              The preview worker discovers the actual sprite is at 0x293AED (+2 bytes).
              The controller calls update_sprite_offset(0x293AEB, 0x293AED).
              
              Expected:
              - Display text should update from "0x293AEB (F1938)" to "0x293AED (F1938)"
              - Internal data offset should update from 0x293AEB to 0x293AED (already works)
              
              Current behavior (bug):
              - Display text remains "0x293AEB (F1938)" (WRONG)
              - Internal data updates correctly (GOOD)
            <Function test_update_sprite_offset_preserves_frame_info>
              Verify that offset update preserves frame information from original name.
              
              Multiple formats should be supported:
              - With frame: "0x293AEB (F1938)" → "0x293AED (F1938)"
              - Without frame: "0x293AEB" → "0x293AED"
            <Function test_update_sprite_offset_handles_missing_frame_info>
              Verify offset update works for sprites without frame info.
              
              Handles names like "0x293AEB" (no frame number in parentheses).

          Regression tests for DropZone feedback loop fixes (Task 4.1.A).
          
          Tests verify that signal blocking prevents infinite loops when

          <Class TestDropZoneFeedbackLoop>
            Tests for DropZone signal feedback loop prevention.
            <Function test_drop_zone_set_no_recursion>
              Verify set_vram_file() doesn't trigger infinite signal loop.
              
              Bug: ExtractTab.set_vram_file() → DropZone.set_file() → signal emitted
                   → lambda in ExtractTab → set_vram_file() → infinite loop
              
              Fix: Use QSignalBlocker in ExtractTab.set_vram_file() to prevent re-emission.
            <Function test_drop_zone_clear_handles_empty>
              Verify clear() handles empty state gracefully (idempotence).
              
              Bug: Calling clear() on empty DropZone could emit signal unnecessarily.
              
              Fix: Idempotence check in DropZone.clear() - return early if already empty.
            <Function test_drop_zone_idempotence>
              Verify set_file() with same path is idempotent.
              
              Bug: Calling set_file() multiple times with same path could emit signal each time.
              
              Fix: Idempotence check in DropZone.set_file() - return early if path unchanged.

          <Class TestSourceTypePreservation>
            Tests for source type preservation during sprite activation.
            
            REGRESSION: Source type (ROM/Mesen/Library) was being lost when activating
            sprites, causing category confusion when multiple sources have the same offset.
            
            These tests verify behavior through signals and observable view state rather
            than accessing private controller attributes.
            <Function test_sprite_activated_preserves_source_type_mesen>
              Source type 'mesen' should be preserved when sprite is activated.
              
              Bug: _on_sprite_activated received source_type but didn't pass it to
              set_offset(), causing source type to not be updated.

        <Module test_thumbnail_mismatch_regression.py>
          <Function test_thumbnail_generation_uses_stale_data>
            Reproduction test for thumbnail mismatch.
            
            Scenario:
            1. Controller is at offset A with valid data for A.
            2. User switches to offset B.
            3. Controller updates current_offset to B, but hasn't received new data yet.
            4. Asset browser requests thumbnail for B.
            5. Controller generates thumbnail using STALE data from A because it thinks
               current_tile_data matches the current_offset.

      <Module test_tile_identity_end_to_end.py>
        End-to-end tests for tile identity preservation through the overlay workflow.
        
        These tests trace a single tile's identity from ROM offset through:
        1. Temp PNG creation
        2. Grid slicing (TilePosition established)
        3. Canvas placement
        4. Overlay sampling
        5. Byte offset patching
        6. Verification that ROM offset matches original
        
        Also includes regression test for the "Apply + Rearrange = Silent Data Loss" bug.
        <Class TestTileIdentityEndToEnd>
          Verify tile identity is preserved through the complete workflow.
          <Function test_tile_identity_preserved_through_overlay_workflow>
            Trace TilePosition(1, 2) through the entire workflow:
            
            1. Grid slicing creates TilePosition(1, 2) with original pixel value 96
            2. User places tile at canvas position (0, 0) - different from source
            3. Overlay is applied, sampling at canvas position (0, 0)
            4. Modified tile is stored with key TilePosition(1, 2)
            5. get_arrangement_result returns modified_tiles[TilePosition(1, 2)]
            6. Verify the tile at physical position (1, 2) was modified, not (0, 0)
          <Function test_byte_offset_calculation_matches_rom_layout>
            Verify that _update_tile_data_from_modified_tiles patches the correct byte offset.
            
            TilePosition(1, 2) with tiles_per_row=4:
            - tile_idx = 1 * 4 + 2 = 6
            - byte_offset = 6 * 32 = 192
            
            The patched bytes should be at data[192:224], not anywhere else.
        <Class TestApplyThenRearrangeDataLoss>
          Test that overlay changes survive arrangement changes (regression tests).
          <Function test_rearrange_after_apply_preserves_modified_tiles>
            Verify that rearranging tiles after applying overlay does NOT lose the changes.
            
            Workflow: Apply overlay → Rearrange tiles → Accept dialog → modified_tiles present
          <Function test_add_tile_after_apply_preserves_modified_tiles>
            Verify that adding a tile after applying overlay does NOT lose the changes.
            
            Workflow: Apply overlay → Add tile → Accept dialog → modified_tiles present
          <Function test_remove_tile_after_apply_preserves_modified_tiles>
            Verify that removing a tile after applying overlay does NOT lose the changes.
            
            Workflow: Apply overlay → Remove tile → Accept dialog → modified_tiles present

          <Class TestSlackSpaceDetection>

            <Function test_start_at_eof_returns_zero>
              Verify slack detection at EOF returns 0.
            <Function test_start_past_eof_returns_zero>
              Verify slack detection past EOF returns 0.
            <Function test_mixed_padding_stops_at_first_non_pad>
              Verify slack detection stops at first non-padding byte.
            <Function test_exact_32_bytes_slack>
              Verify exactly 32 bytes of slack is detected correctly.
            <Function test_exactly_max_slack_size>
              Verify MAX_SLACK_SIZE is respected exactly.
            <Function test_zero_padding_detected>
              Verify 0x00 padding is detected as slack.
            <Function test_mixed_ff_and_zero_only_counts_first_type>
              Verify only consistent padding type is counted.
            <Function test_no_slack_when_first_byte_is_data>
              Verify no slack detected when first byte isn't padding.
            <Function test_negative_offset_treated_as_invalid>
              Verify negative offset doesn't crash (returns 0 or handles gracefully).
          <Class TestSlackBoundaryEdgeCases>
            Tests for slack boundary edge cases (31, 32, 33 bytes).
            <Function test_31_bytes_slack_all_used>
              Verify 31 bytes of slack can be fully used (under max_slack_usage=32).
            <Function test_33_bytes_slack_detection>
              Verify 33 bytes of slack is detected (but inject caps at 32).
          <Class TestEffectiveLimitCalculation>
            Tests for effective limit calculation logic.
            
            The effective limit is calculated as:
                effective_limit = original_size + min(slack_size, max_slack_usage)
            
            where max_slack_usage = 32 bytes by default.
            <Function test_effective_limit_no_slack>
              Verify effective limit equals original size when no slack.
            <Function test_effective_limit_with_slack_under_max>
              Verify effective limit includes all slack when under max.
            <Function test_effective_limit_with_slack_at_max>
              Verify effective limit caps slack at max_slack_usage.
            <Function test_effective_limit_exactly_at_boundary>
              Verify effective limit calculation at exact boundary.
            <Function test_overflow_detection_one_byte_over>
              Verify overflow detected when exceeding effective limit by 1 byte.
            <Function test_no_overflow_at_exact_limit>
              Verify no overflow when exactly at effective limit.
          <Class TestOverflowProtection>
            Tests for overflow protection logic.
            
            These tests verify the overflow detection formula:
                overflow_bytes = compressed_size - effective_limit
                if compressed_size > effective_limit and not force:
                    reject with error message
            <Function test_overflow_detection_formula>
              Verify overflow calculation matches expected formula.
            <Function test_error_message_contains_overflow_amount>
              Verify error message format includes useful information.
          <Class TestForceInjectionMode>
            Tests for force injection mode behavior.
            
            When force=True, injection proceeds even with overflow,
            but logs warnings about overwritten bytes.
            <Function test_force_mode_allows_overflow>
              Verify force mode calculation allows injection despite overflow.
            <Function test_non_force_mode_rejects_overflow>
              Verify non-force mode rejects overflow.
            <Function test_force_mode_overwrite_calculation>
              Verify overwrite range calculation in force mode.
          <Class TestZeroLengthDataProtection>
            Tests for zero-length and empty data handling.
            <Function test_empty_tile_data_detection>
              Verify empty tile data is detected before injection.
            <Function test_non_empty_tile_data_accepted>
              Verify non-empty tile data is accepted.
          <Class TestRawCompressionModeBoundaries>
            Tests for RAW (uncompressed) injection mode boundaries.
            
            In RAW mode:
            - original_size = len(tile_data) (new data size is the slot size)
            - slack_size = 0 (no slack detection for raw)
            - No compression applied
            <Function test_raw_mode_slot_size_equals_tile_data>
              Verify RAW mode uses tile data size as slot size.
            <Function test_raw_mode_no_compression_ratio>
              Verify RAW mode has 0% compression ratio.
            <Function test_raw_mode_size_comparison>
              Verify RAW mode compares new size against original slot.
          <Class TestPreserveExistingParameter>
            Tests for the preserve_existing parameter in inject_sprite_to_rom.
            
            When preserve_existing=True and output_path exists, the injector should
            read from output_path instead of copying from rom_path. This preserves
            prior injections when batch injecting into the same output ROM.
            <Function test_preserve_existing_reads_from_output_path>
              When preserve_existing=True and output exists, read from output.
            <Function test_preserve_existing_false_copies_from_source>
              When preserve_existing=False, copy from source ROM to output.
          <Class TestROMInjectorIntegration>
            Integration tests for ROM injector public API.

            validating slack space detection, header operations, and checksum updates.
            <Function test_read_write_header_round_trip>
              Verify header can be read, modified, and checksums recalculated.
              
              Integration test: Reads ROM header, modifies data, recalculates checksum,
              verifies the resulting ROM has valid checksum relationship.
            <Function test_slack_space_detected_and_usable>

              Integration test: Creates ROM with slack space after sprite data,
              detects slack via _detect_slack_space, verifies correct amount detected.
            <Function test_slack_capped_at_max_usage_in_limit_calc>

              verifies the 32-byte cap is applied correctly.
            <Function test_copy_rom_creates_independent_file>
              Verify copy_rom_for_injection creates an independent copy.
              
              Integration test: Creates source ROM, copies to output, modifies output,
              verifies source is unchanged.
            <Function test_zero_padding_slack_detection>
              Verify 0x00 padding is correctly detected as slack space.
              
              Integration test: ROM with 0x00 padding (common in some games),
              verifies detection algorithm handles this padding type.
            <Function test_mixed_padding_stops_at_type_change>
              Verify slack detection stops when padding type changes.
              
              Integration test: ROM with mixed 0xFF then 0x00 padding,
              verifies only first consistent run is counted.

        <Module test_sprite_reassembler.py>
          Tests for SpriteReassembler SNES tile arrangement.
          
          Verifies that the reassembler correctly handles SNES 16-tile row stride
          when extracting tiles from decompressed data.
          
          SNES sprite tile layout:
          - 16x16 (2x2 tiles): [0][1] / [16][17]
          - 32x32 (4x4 tiles): [0][1][2][3] / [16][17][18][19] / [32][33][34][35] / [48][49][50][51]
          <Class TestSNESTileArrangement>

              16x16 sprite should read tiles 0, 1, 16, 17 not 0, 1, 2, 3.
            <Function test_16x16_sprite_with_nonzero_base_tile>
              16x16 sprite starting at tile 4 should read tiles 4, 5, 20, 21.
            <Function test_32x32_sprite_uses_stride>
              32x32 sprite should use 16-tile row stride for all 4 rows.
            <Function test_out_of_bounds_tile_zero_padded>
              Tiles that exceed data bounds should be zero-padded.

        <Class TestSA1AddressTranslation>
          Test SA-1 address translation (Kirby Super Star, Super Mario RPG, etc.)

          docs/mesen2/03_GAME_MAPPING_KIRBY_SA1.md
          <Function test_sa1_to_file_offset_basic>
            Test SA-1 address translation with documented example from SPRITE_LEARNINGS.

            Test execute requires force=True when warnings exist.

            Test execute produces modified tile images.
        <Class TestApplyOperationPaletteQuantization>
          Test Apply operation palette quantization.
          <Function test_quantize_to_palette>
            Test that pixels are quantized to nearest palette color.
          <Function test_perceptual_color_matching_preserves_vivid_colors>
            Test that vivid colors are not mapped to pale equivalents.
            
            Bug: Simple Euclidean RGB distance often maps vivid colors to paler
            versions because it doesn't account for human perception. Green
            sensitivity is highest, followed by red, then blue.
            
            This test verifies that a vivid red (255, 0, 0) is matched to the
            vivid red in the palette, not to a paler red that might be
            mathematically closer.
          <Function test_perceptual_color_matching_saturated_blue>
            Test perceptual matching for saturated blue.
            
            Human eyes are least sensitive to blue, so a pure saturated blue
            should strongly prefer other saturated blues over desaturated ones.

      <Module test_checksum_disambiguation.py>
        Tests for checksum disambiguation when multiple games share the same checksum.
        
        Bug: Three Kirby games share checksum 0xBF51:
        - "KIRBY SUPER STAR" (Europe_Alt)
        - "KIRBY SUPER DELUXE" (Europe_FunPak)
        - "KIRBY'S FUN PAK" (Europe_BF51)
        
        Current behavior: First match wins (arbitrary).
        Expected behavior: Use title scoring to disambiguate.
        <Class TestSingleChecksumMatch>
          Tests for games with unique checksums (should work as before).
          <Function test_single_checksum_match_is_authoritative>
            Single checksum match wins even if title doesn't match exactly.
          <Function test_single_checksum_match_wins_over_title>
            Checksum match should win even with slightly different title.
        <Class TestMultipleChecksumMatches>
          Tests for games that share the same checksum (the bug fix).
          <Function test_multiple_checksum_matches_use_title_scoring>
            When multiple games share a checksum, use title scoring to disambiguate.
          <Function test_kirby_super_star_title_selects_correct_game>
            Title 'KIRBY SUPER STAR' + checksum 0xBF51 should select KIRBY SUPER STAR.
          <Function test_kirby_super_deluxe_title_selects_correct_game>
            Title 'KIRBY SUPER DELUXE' + checksum 0xBF51 should select KIRBY SUPER DELUXE.
        <Class TestTitleScoringPrecedence>
          Tests to verify title scoring precedence: exact(100) > substring(50) > equivalence(25).
          <Function test_exact_match_beats_substring>
            Exact title match (100) should beat substring match (50).
          <Function test_equivalence_match_is_used_for_disambiguation>
            Equivalence patterns (FUN PAK ↔ SUPER STAR) should contribute to scoring.
        <Class TestGetGameSpritesDisambiguation>
          Tests for get_game_sprites() which has the same bug.
          <Function test_get_game_sprites_disambiguates_by_title>
            get_game_sprites() should also use title scoring for disambiguation.
          <Function test_get_game_sprites_super_star_title>
            get_game_sprites() with 'KIRBY SUPER STAR' title should select correct config.
        <Class TestNoChecksumMatch>
          Tests for fallback behavior when no checksum matches.
          <Function test_title_only_match_uses_scoring>
            When no checksum matches, title scoring should be used.
          <Function test_no_match_returns_none>
            When neither checksum nor title matches, return None.

      <Module test_decompression_bomb.py>
        Tests for HAL decompression bomb prevention.
        
        Bug: `decompress_from_rom()` reads entire decompressed file into memory
        BEFORE checking size, allowing potential DoS via memory exhaustion.
        
        Expected behavior: Check file size BEFORE reading to prevent bomb.

      <Module test_hal_golden.py>
        Golden HAL tests - verify compression behavior against recorded checksums.
        
        These tests do NOT require real exhal/inhal binaries. They verify that:
        1. Mock HAL produces deterministic output
        2. Real HAL (when available) produces expected output matching recorded checksums
        
        Usage:
            # Run golden tests with mocks (always available)
            uv run pytest tests/test_hal_golden.py -m golden_hal -v
        
            # Regenerate golden data with real HAL
            SPRITEPAL_EXHAL_PATH=/path/to/exhal uv run pytest tests/test_hal_golden.py --regenerate-golden -v
        <Class TestMockHALDeterminism>

      <Module test_hal_parsing.py>
        Tests for HAL compression parsing.
        
        This module tests the HALParser.parse_compressed_size() method
        to verify it correctly parses HAL compression streams and calculates
        compressed block sizes.
        
        HAL Compression Format Reference (from exhal compress.c):
        - No header - starts directly with command bytes
        - Command encoding:
          - If (cmd & 0xE0) == 0xE0: Long command
            - command = (cmd >> 2) & 0x07
            - length = (((cmd & 0x03) << 8) | next_byte) + 1
          - Else: Short command
            - command = cmd >> 5
            - length = (cmd & 0x1F) + 1
        - Commands:
          - 0: Raw bytes (length bytes follow in stream)
          - 1: 8-bit RLE (1 byte follows)
          - 2: 16-bit RLE (2 bytes follow)
          - 3: Sequence RLE (1 byte follows)
          - 4,7: Forward backref (2 bytes offset follow)
          - 5: Rotated backref (2 bytes offset follow)
          - 6: Backward backref (2 bytes offset follow)
        - 0xFF terminates the stream
        <Class TestConservativeFallback>
          Tests for fallback heuristic improvements.
          <Function test_fallback_uses_64_byte_threshold>
            Verify fallback requires 64 consecutive bytes, not 32.
          <Function test_fallback_default_is_8kb>
            Verify fallback default is 8KB when no padding found.
        <Class TestCompressionRatioValidation>
          Tests for compression ratio validation.
          <Function test_low_ratio_warning_logged>
            Check that unusually low compression ratios trigger rejection.
        <Class TestShortCommands>
          Test short command format parsing (5-bit length).

          <Function test_raw_bytes_max_short>

          <Function test_8bit_rle>

          <Function test_16bit_rle>
            Test parsing 16-bit RLE command.
          <Function test_sequence_rle>
            Test parsing sequence RLE command.

        <Class TestLongCommands>

      <Module test_palette_utils.py>
        Tests for core/palette_utils.py - SNES palette conversion and quantization.
        <Class TestSnesPaletteToRgb>
          Tests for snes_palette_to_rgb function.
          <Function test_converts_bgr555_to_rgb_full_8bit_range>
            BGR555 max value (31) should produce full 8-bit value (255), not 248.
            
            The correct 5-bit to 8-bit conversion is: (value << 3) | (value >> 2)
            This scales 31 (max 5-bit) to 255 (max 8-bit), not 248.
            Example: 31 << 3 = 248, 31 >> 2 = 7, 248 | 7 = 255
            
            Bug impact: Incomplete scaling produces muted colors (248 instead of 255).
          <Function test_passes_through_rgb_triplets>
            RGB triplets (list format) should pass through unchanged.
          <Function test_handles_mixed_formats>
            Should handle mixed BGR555 integers and RGB triplets.
          <Function test_black_is_zero>
            Black (0x0000) should convert to (0, 0, 0).
          <Function test_handles_empty_palette>
            Empty palette should return empty list.
        <Class TestBgr555ToRgb>
          Tests for bgr555_to_rgb utility function.
          <Function test_full_values_scale_to_255>
            Max 5-bit values (31) should scale to max 8-bit (255).
          <Function test_zero_values>
            Zero values should stay zero.
          <Function test_mid_values>
            Mid-range 5-bit values (16) should scale correctly.
            
            16 << 3 = 128, 16 >> 2 = 4, 128 | 4 = 132
          <Function test_low_values>
            Low 5-bit value (1) should scale correctly.
            
            1 << 3 = 8, 1 >> 2 = 0, 8 | 0 = 8
        <Class TestQuantizeToPalette>
          Tests for quantize_to_palette function.
          <Function test_quantizes_solid_color_to_nearest_palette_entry>
            Solid color image should map to nearest palette color.
          <Function test_transparent_pixels_map_to_index_zero>
            Transparent pixels should always map to palette index 0.
          <Function test_mixed_transparency>
            Image with both transparent and opaque pixels.
          <Function test_nearest_color_matching>
            Should find nearest color by Euclidean distance.
          <Function test_output_has_correct_palette>
            Output image should have the specified palette embedded.
          <Function test_converts_rgb_input_to_rgba>
            RGB input should be converted to RGBA internally.
          <Function test_tile_aligned_image>
            8x8 tile-aligned images should work correctly.
          <Function test_opaque_pixel_never_quantized_to_index_0>
            Opaque pixels should never map to index 0 (transparency index).
            
            Index 0 is reserved for transparency in SNES sprites. Even if an opaque
            pixel's color is closest to palette[0], it should map to the next-closest
            color (index 1+) to preserve visibility in-game.
        <Class TestPaletteUtilsIntegration>
          Integration tests combining both functions.

            Even with color mappings, the nearest-color fallback should exclude
            index 0 for opaque pixels.
        <Class TestBgr555RoundtripConversion>
          Tests for BGR555 roundtrip conversion (RGB -> BGR555 -> RGB).
          <Function test_roundtrip_conversion>
            Test that extraction and injection are approximately inverse operations.
            
            Note: Due to 8-bit to 5-bit quantization, exact roundtrip is not possible.
            The tolerance is +-7 (since 255/31 ≈ 8.2, values can vary by up to 7).

      <Module test_quantization_parity.py>
        Tests for quantization parity between preview and injection.
        
        Verifies that:
        1. Preview and injection use the same transparency threshold (WYSIWYG)
        2. Semi-transparent pixels (alpha 1-127) are treated as transparent
        3. All quantization paths use perceptual LAB distance
        4. ColorQuantizer uses the centralized threshold constant
        <Class TestTransparencyThresholdParity>
          Tests for transparency threshold consistency.

          <Module test_frame_mapping_controller.py>
            Tests for FrameMappingController selected_entry_ids filtering.

            <Class TestGetCaptureResultFiltering>

            <Class TestInjectMappingEntryFiltering>
              Tests that inject_mapping filters entries by selected_entry_ids, not rom_offset.
              
              Bug: inject_mapping at line 690 filters by rom_offset which can match wrong entries
              when multiple frames share ROM offsets. Should filter by selected_entry_ids instead.
              <Function test_inject_mapping_uses_selected_entry_ids_not_rom_offset>
                Injection should filter by selected_entry_ids, not rom_offset.
                
                Scenario: Two entries with different IDs but SAME rom_offset (shared tile).
                If filtering by rom_offset, both entries are included (wrong).
                If filtering by selected_entry_ids, only the selected entry is included (correct).
            <Class TestInjectMappingFlipHandling>
              Tests that inject_mapping correctly handles entry-level flips.
              
              Bug: Tile position calculation ignores entry flip_h/flip_v flags.
              CaptureRenderer correctly mirrors tile positions for flipped entries,
              but inject_mapping extracts tiles from wrong positions.
              
              Additionally, extracted tile data must be counter-flipped because:
              - CaptureRenderer renders tiles in "screen appearance" (flipped)
              - ROM stores tiles in unflipped form (SNES hardware applies flip at display)
              - Injecting screen-appearance data = SNES applies flip again = double-flipped = wrong
              <Function test_tile_positions_mirror_when_flip_h>
                With flip_h=True, tile at pos_x=0 should appear at right edge.
                
                For a 16x16 sprite with flip_h=True:
                - Tile at (pos_x=0, pos_y=0) should be at screen position (entry.x + 8, entry.y)
                - Tile at (pos_x=1, pos_y=0) should be at screen position (entry.x + 0, entry.y)
                
                To verify correct behavior:
                - Create AI frame with distinct colors in each quadrant
                - After injection, check that tile 0 (pos_x=0, vram_addr=0x1000) contains
                  the RIGHT side of the AI frame (because flip_h mirrors positions)
                
                BUG: Currently calculates screen_x = entry.x + pos_x * 8, ignoring flip.
              <Function test_tile_data_counter_flipped_for_flip_h>
                Extracted tiles must be counter-flipped before ROM injection.
                
                When flip_h=True:
                - CaptureRenderer renders tiles horizontally flipped (screen appearance)
                - We extract from screen appearance (flipped)
                - Before injection, we must flip back (counter-flip)
                - SNES will re-apply flip_h at display time → correct result
                
                BUG: Currently injects screen-appearance data without counter-flip.
                SNES applies flip_h again → double-flipped → incorrect.
            <Class TestInjectMappingScale>
              Tests that inject_mapping applies scale transform to AI image.
              
              Bug: Preview applies scale via workbench_canvas._generate_preview() but
              inject_mapping only applies flip transforms, not scale.
              <Function test_inject_mapping_applies_scale>
                Injection should resize AI image when mapping.scale != 1.0.
                
                BUG: Currently inject_mapping ignores mapping.scale, only applying flips.
                The preview shows scaled image but injection uses original size.

                Expected: used_fallback is True and falls back to rom_offset filtering.
              <Function test_emits_stale_warning_signal_on_fallback>
                Emits stale_entries_warning signal when fallback is used.
                
                Scenario: Entry IDs are stale, triggering fallback.
                Expected: stale_entries_warning signal is emitted with frame_id.
              <Function test_returns_false_when_no_selected_entry_ids>
                Returns used_fallback=False when game frame has no stored selection.
                
                Scenario: Game frame has empty selected_entry_ids (no filtering applied).
                Expected: used_fallback is False, all entries returned.
              <Function test_returns_none_for_missing_game_frame>
                Returns (None, False) for non-existent game frame ID.
              <Function test_returns_none_when_no_project>
                Returns (None, False) when no project is loaded.
            <Class TestRawSlotDetection>
              Tests for RAW slot size detection.
              <Function test_raw_slot_detection_finds_padding_boundary>
                Detects slot size by finding all-zero padding after tiles.
              <Function test_raw_slot_detection_finds_ff_padding>
                Detects slot size by finding all-0xFF padding after tiles.

            <Class TestRawInjectionSlotRespect>
              Tests that RAW injection respects detected slot size.
              <Function test_raw_injection_respects_detected_slot_size>
                RAW injection limits tiles to detected slot size.
                
                Scenario: Capture has 5 tiles, ROM slot only has room for 3.
                Expected: Only 3 tiles worth of data extracted from canvas.
                
                Note: The grid layout may use 2x2=4 slots for 3 tiles, but only
                3 vram_addrs are processed (the 4th slot is empty/transparent).
              <Function test_raw_fallback_when_no_boundary_detected>
                RAW injection uses captured count when no boundary detected.
                
                Scenario: ROM has no padding boundary (continuous data).
                Expected: All captured tiles are injected (fallback behavior).
            <Class TestInjectionRollback>
